  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f69fa6c1-5c91-473e-9ba7-08bdbe41e00e'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer304960374733127223">Tall, dark, and mysterious—Ryder Black is everything a girl wants. The catch? He’s trouble. Naturally, he’s irresistibly charming. Surprisingly, he’s impressively academic, too.   <span id="freeText304960374733127223" style="display:none">Tall, dark, and mysterious—Ryder Black is everything a girl wants. The catch? He’s trouble. Naturally, he’s irresistibly charming. Surprisingly, he’s impressively academic, too. But it’s his knack for getting into fights that makes him notorious. <br /> <br />Dorky, clumsy, and just plain odd—April Hale talks like Yoda, eats her food based on the day of the week, and prefers binge watching TV shows to partying. She has also spent the past few years eavesdropping on the Blacks’ morning fights. It was her daily routine. Until that one morning that Ryder catches her looking into his bedroom window… and she becomes all but anonymous in his eyes. <br /> <br />Hell-bent on making contact, Ryder gets a sneak peek into the quirky world of April when she stuffs all of her fingers in her mouth and faints the first time he talks to her. <br /> <br />She’s unusual. He’s captivated. <br /> <br />In this delightfully wacky and fun story, we discover that sometimes what makes us outcasts from the world are the very things that make us special. Join April and Ryder in their journey to discovering more about life… and about each other. It will give you butterflies in the stomach, tickle your funny bones, and pull at your heartstrings until the very last page.</span>

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4417768612497519533">This was so freaking, <b>ADORABLE.</b> <br/><br/>This is another one of those 'boy next door' stories. But this one is <i>completely</i> different. <br/><br/>April Hale has got to be the quirkiest oddball I have ever read about. She would rather watch her Star Wars or Big Bang Theory DVDs than go and make friends. <b>I want to be her friend.</b> But here's the thing: she has a disorder. It's called Asperger's. It makes it harder for her to notice people's emotions. She doesn't know what <i>love</i> feels like. She's not used to compliments. S</span>
  <span id="freeText4417768612497519533" style="display:none">This was so freaking, <b>ADORABLE.</b> <br /><br />This is another one of those 'boy next door' stories. But this one is <i>completely</i> different. <br /><br />April Hale has got to be the quirkiest oddball I have ever read about. She would rather watch her Star Wars or Big Bang Theory DVDs than go and make friends. <b>I want to be her friend.</b> But here's the thing: she has a disorder. It's called Asperger's. It makes it harder for her to notice people's emotions. She doesn't know what <i>love</i> feels like. She's not used to compliments. She's <i>
  <b>different.</b>
</i><br /><br />April's neighbors, the Blacks, is a family falling apart. They argue loudly every, single morning, they're basically April's alarm clock. The cause: Ryder Black. Bad boy. Troublemaker. The freak of the the school. You should stay out of Ryder's way. Seriously. And he isn't one of those very cliché womanizers. Just a very snarky street fighter. Well, one day, Ryder's parents kick him out of the house. Then he asks April a question that could change both of their lives: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"March, will you let me stay in your room?"</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Ryder didn't even get her name right. They form a sorta-friendship from there and it blossoms it to something great more into the book. <br /><br />And can I just add how awesome April's parents are? I just love them! <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Both of my parents looked at each other and then nodded slowly. "Good answer," my father said. "And do you..."<br />There was a pause that went on longer than would have been normal. <br />"Dang it, Meredith [April's Mom], I'm not good at being an Intimidating Father Towards His Daughter's Boyfriend."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />See what I mean? <br /><br />This is a hilarious coming of age story about the surprises of falling in love. It was sweet and had some unpredictable scenes and I JUST LOVED IT ALL. <br /><br />Find this fantastic story <a href="http://www.wattpad.com/story/3710071-the-quirky-tale-of-april-hale" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a></span>

<div id="review_1125769515" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1125769515" />
    <a title="Freya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24309724-freya"><img alt="Freya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460120640p2/24309724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1125769515?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Freya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Freya" href="/user/show/24309724-freya">Freya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18583911-the-quirky-tale-of-april-hale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24309724-freya?shelf=wattpad">wattpad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1125769515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13489211470786963281"><b>Friendly Advice</b>: If you don't want to know anything about this story, you may not read my review. <br/>But if you want to know more about the concept and the whole idea of the book, go ahead. (:<br/><br/><br/>Wow. Surprisingly it was really well written(I don't see it that often) and I really loved how it was just different from so many books but was also reminding me of many other stories I know. I mean think of the idea: two neighbors living side by side for 10 years, only seperated by walls and 10 meters, each o</span>
  <span id="freeText13489211470786963281" style="display:none"><b>Friendly Advice</b>: If you don't want to know anything about this story, you may not read my review. <br />But if you want to know more about the concept and the whole idea of the book, go ahead. (:<br /><br /><br />Wow. Surprisingly it was really well written(I don't see it that often) and I really loved how it was just different from so many books but was also reminding me of many other stories I know. I mean think of the idea: two neighbors living side by side for 10 years, only seperated by walls and 10 meters, each one 'stalking' the other but they're unaware that the one is doing the same thing as the other.<br /><br />Back to the referring to other stories. <br />Did she read <i>Shades of Grey</i>? April often bit her lower lipas a nercous habit! And she didn't want to get touched by another human being other than her family(okay she's the SHE and not the HE -alas Fifty Shades- in the book and it's because of her condition, but yeah).<br />Oh gosh what were the other books or movies I thought about while reading? … Oh yeah another one is <i>The Boy Next Door</i>. A boy amd a girl the same age living next door and one stalking the other but at least one of them doesn't know the other one is kind of doing the same. <br />I even thought of <i>TFiOS</i> because of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the cancer thingy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>!! <br /><br />Well I liked the way the author always did that little notes at the end of every chapter on wattpad and I loved how she was so well informed about the whole <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[autism syndrome and could even be realistic abput it since she knew someone who had it <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br />I also liked all the little comments about movies or TV shows or even science(I'm really NOT into science and didn't understand at least half of it). This gave the story even more personality.<br />And my respect to you, you lady, to not even be into Star Wars (and many other movies and so on you spoke about) but knowing so much about them!<br /><br />The ending is a little sad, to be honest, but it rounds it up perfectly and smooth and now I can't wait to go into the sequel, even if it's not even close to being finished yet. (:<br /><br /><br />ps: Wow I think this is my longest reciew on GR by now!!<br />ps2: I will also upload this review on my blog( <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.soundofavoice.wordpress.com">www.soundofavoice.wordpress.com</a> ) soon.<br /><br /><b>Update:</b> My review is now on <a href="http://soundofavoice.wordpress.com/2014/12/08/the-quirky-tale-of-april-hale-von-demonicblackcat-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13489211470786963281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648138274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14055422187785332104">Let me just start by saying that this started as a story on Wattpad before being discovered and picked up by a small publishing company...so I didn't really know what to expect.<br/><br/>SO FREAKING AMAZING. The fact that this romantic comedy has an autistic teenager as its heroine is amazing enough--but when you throw in how hilarious and touching it is, I couldn't get enough. There were SO MANY lines I had to go back and read again just because they were so good. April's condition makes interacting with</span>
  <span id="freeText14055422187785332104" style="display:none">Let me just start by saying that this started as a story on Wattpad before being discovered and picked up by a small publishing company...so I didn't really know what to expect.<br /><br />SO FREAKING AMAZING. The fact that this romantic comedy has an autistic teenager as its heroine is amazing enough--but when you throw in how hilarious and touching it is, I couldn't get enough. There were SO MANY lines I had to go back and read again just because they were so good. April's condition makes interacting with others and understanding subtext difficult, but she is so much more than that. One of the best female teen narrators I've read in awhile.<br /><br />Fair warning--there are quite a few grammatical errors in this one...maybe because of the small-scale publishing thing? Or maybe English isn't the author's first language (her bios say she lives in Indonesia)? There were some subject/verb disagreements and some odd prepositional choices...but if an anal-retentive English teacher like me caught them all and still gave the book 5 stars, I don't think they'll bother too many other people.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14055422187785332104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1649139562" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1649139562" />
    <a title="Brittany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10854693-brittany"><img alt="Brittany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341974923p2/10854693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1649139562?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany" href="/user/show/10854693-brittany">Brittany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1649139562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6777997203167999397">So many people don't know about this book, and that is a travesty. <br/><br/>At the heart of it, this book is a love story, but it's really about the many languages people speak without knowing it, and how we share our feelings. This book shows how even with huge barriers, there are certain things in life that are universal like love affection and forgiveness and grief. <br/><br/>April is a character that I will never forget and long as I live. She lives in a world that makes zero sense to her, and you keep rooting</span>
  <span id="freeText6777997203167999397" style="display:none">So many people don't know about this book, and that is a travesty. <br /><br />At the heart of it, this book is a love story, but it's really about the many languages people speak without knowing it, and how we share our feelings. This book shows how even with huge barriers, there are certain things in life that are universal like love affection and forgiveness and grief. <br /><br />April is a character that I will never forget and long as I live. She lives in a world that makes zero sense to her, and you keep rooting for every victory that comes her way. <br /><br />I have read a lot of characters who are on the spectrum, my favorite being Caitlin in Mockingbird by Erskine, until now. April is the epitome of thoughtfulness and curiosity while blatantly navigating her condition while demanding a normal life that includes love.<br /><br />You'd have to be dead inside to not be moved by this book, it made my heart melt and it had me laughing and snorting on every page. <br /><br />Published by a tiny press, there are some editing errors, but I don't care. I think it's perfection. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6777997203167999397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1647095739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8331309599195807143">Not impressed. If April was an Aspie, the author didnt do her research. If felt cruel and mocking and not relatable at all. April liked guys, wasn't intelligent, was prone to fainting, etc. If anything, she was guy obsessed and thats it. Of course all aspies are different, but I have never heard that we are prone to fainting. <br/><br/>Same with not knowing her way home. If anything, the routine of going the same way to and from school easy day (because we all love routines, right?) would ensure she could</span>
  <span id="freeText8331309599195807143" style="display:none">Not impressed. If April was an Aspie, the author didnt do her research. If felt cruel and mocking and not relatable at all. April liked guys, wasn't intelligent, was prone to fainting, etc. If anything, she was guy obsessed and thats it. Of course all aspies are different, but I have never heard that we are prone to fainting. <br /><br />Same with not knowing her way home. If anything, the routine of going the same way to and from school easy day (because we all love routines, right?) would ensure she could get home safely. I know the way to my house from school, what teenager doesnt?<br /><br />Aspies out there, let me set a rule: Dont invite guys into your room or bed. This does not result in a happy ending. Be safe. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10769714251445908540">I absolutely LOVED the book. I found it on Wattpad, and it's by far the best story I've read so far. And that's saying A LOT! The book is VERY enjoyable, fun, humorous, and just flat out amazing. The characters are very well developed, and are all unique and special in their own way. Be prepared to laugh out loud, cry, scream, squeal, blush, and everything in between. Great story written by an amazing writer. CONGRADULATIONS on being published!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1474993708" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1474993708" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42159657-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443619758p2/42159657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1474993708?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/42159657-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1474993708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17815396900390099294">Whenever I look for a book, I try to look for a main character that I would find likable since it is very difficult to like a book in which you don't like the character that the story is about. In The Quirky Tale of April Hale, I found April more likable than most female main characters of other books I've read. She is oblivious to the bad things of the world, and her personality is very similar to a child, which is very difficult to find in a character. She was absolutely ADORABLE. She also has</span>
  <span id="freeText17815396900390099294" style="display:none">Whenever I look for a book, I try to look for a main character that I would find likable since it is very difficult to like a book in which you don't like the character that the story is about. In The Quirky Tale of April Hale, I found April more likable than most female main characters of other books I've read. She is oblivious to the bad things of the world, and her personality is very similar to a child, which is very difficult to find in a character. She was absolutely ADORABLE. She also has this mental illness called Aspergers (a type of autism) which makes it difficult for her to understand people's emotions. This books basically tells us what the life of an autistic person is like, and it really got me interested and looking through Wikipedia researching all types of autisms and their symptoms and all that stuff. I felt like I was learning new information while reading the book, and that is something I really like about books like these because I can learn a lot more than what they teach me at school.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17815396900390099294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12288684464335438095" style="display:none">Huge editing errors, very poor writing. That being said I could see the potential kin this plot. The author just was not quite experienced enough to make it work and bring out that full potential. Because this is an unexperienced author with a good idea, I gave it 2 stars. With a little more practice and help (especially with editing) this author could do really well though, so I encourage the author to keep writing and learning. As for other readers, if you have only read a few books and can get over bad editing, you may enjoy this book. If you are like me and have read many books so your standards are high, you may want to take a pass.<br />S.S.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12878912-jadeshea?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12878912-jadeshea?shelf=wattpad">wattpad</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920998702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10125793221005735824">Found on Wattpad.<br/><br/><br/>The story begins with April Hale being the social inept nerd at her school. She only has two friends, who she isn't really even that close to. And her twin brother is the complete opposite of her. He's the popular jock guy at school. Things change for April when the bad boy who lives next door gets kicked out of his house, and she lets him stay in her room. These two actually start to form a friendship, and develop feelings for her. But April has a condition that makes it very h</span>
  <span id="freeText10125793221005735824" style="display:none">Found on Wattpad.<br /><br /><br />The story begins with April Hale being the social inept nerd at her school. She only has two friends, who she isn't really even that close to. And her twin brother is the complete opposite of her. He's the popular jock guy at school. Things change for April when the bad boy who lives next door gets kicked out of his house, and she lets him stay in her room. These two actually start to form a friendship, and develop feelings for her. But April has a condition that makes it very hard for her to understand the social norms, and people's feelings. You add this and the bad boy who is having family problems into the mix and you have a whole lot of drama. <br /><br />This story was something I found on wattpad. It wasn't at all like I thought it was going to be. I thought it was going to be your typical "nerd falls for bad boy" type of thing. But I was very wrong. It is the nerd falling for the bad boy, but April isn't just a nerd. She as a form of autism that makes it hard for her to communicate with people, and understand their feelings. And the bad boy next door to her slowly starts to fall for her. Now I have to say there are only two things I didn't like about this story. One of them is towards the end I sort of felt like Ryder was giving up on April in a way. It was kind of frustrating. And then to see April try so hard to be the person he needs was beautiful. And I really wish we had gotten more out of the epilogue.. Like maybe what happens to them a few years later. <br /><br />Anyways, the other thing I didn't like was the story needed to be edited. Now I normally can deal with this type of thing by just fixing it in my head and moving on quickly. But in this one I had to read several sentences over and over to understand what was going on. Other than that this book was very well written, with a very unique plot line.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10125793221005735824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1489059820" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1489059820" />
    <a title="Anita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5055773-anita"><img alt="Anita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603550135p2/5055773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1489059820?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anita" href="/user/show/5055773-anita">Anita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1489059820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6302275569848785509"><strong>Unique Narrative Perspective.</strong><br/><br/>I picked this book for it's quirky title and the possibility of a quick read. I got much more. Experiencing the story from an Asperger diagnosed teen was an eye opener. Though I have known a few people with this moderate level of diagnosis, I have a new appreciation for the communication and socialization hurdles. This is more than a YA tale, rather a story with struggles from a perspective not often explored in this everyday type of narrative context.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1757734289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14318965946819180043">A story where April the weird,nerdy, and non popular is neighbors with the bad boy. Ryder Black. The boy who always is in trouble but no one really sees how he truly is. What happens when he asks to stay in her room because his dad kicks him out? Will this change both of their lives? I would reccomend this book but the only reason I gave it four stars was because there was quite a bit of cussing, but overall it was a great book. :)</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6Bstl++n8oZNAD5dqWjSS4AU/GjSdRc+IEnRMcjqOEP689+RNx6EJZ4Vm0apyUj3Jgl/Pk59mOofUMmr6w0Gtg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
